## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(P) = 0.17(-1 + P/1.047)(1 - P/10.21)P + 0.17(1 - P/10.21)P + 0.17(1 - e^{-0.097P})P$$

Let me expand this. Let me use $a = 0.17$, $b = 1.047$, $d = 10.21$, $k = 0.097$.

**Term 1:** $a(-1 + P/b)(1 - P/d)P = a(P/b - 1)(1 - P/d)P$
$= a(P/b - P^2/(bd) - 1 + P/d)P$
$= a(P^2/b - P^3/(bd) - P + P^2/d)$

**Term 2:** $a(1 - P/d)P = a(P - P^2/d)$

**Term 3:** $a(1 - e^{-kP})P = a(P - Pe^{-kP})$

Combining Terms 1+2+3:
- $P^3$ coefficient: $-a/(bd)$
- $P^2$ coefficient: $a/b + a/d - a/d = a/b$
- $P$ coefficient: $-a + a + a = a$
- Exponential term: $-aPe^{-kP}$

So GT = $-\frac{a}{bd}P^3 + \frac{a}{b}P^2 + aP - aPe^{-kP}$

This is: **polynomial in P (cubic) plus an exponential term $Pe^{-kP}$**.

The key basis functions are: $P^3$, $P^2$, $P$, and $Pe^{-kP}$ (where $k > 0$, so the exponential decays).

## Candidate Analysis

For a candidate to match, it must contain:
1. A polynomial part up to degree 3 in P
2. A $Pe^{-kP}$ term (with $k > 0$, meaning the exponent coefficient is negative)

Most candidates use rational functions $P^n/(Pc_1 + c_2)$. A rational function like $\frac{P^{n+1}}{Pc_1+c_2}$ can approximate but NOT exactly equal a polynomial for all P. So pure rational + polynomial candidates cannot match.

Candidates with exponential terms like $e^{cP}$: if $c$ is a free constant, we can set $c < 0$ to get $e^{-kP}$. We need terms that can produce $Pe^{-kP}$ and potentially a constant times $e^{-kP}$.

Let me check candidates with exponential terms that also have enough polynomial flexibility:

**Candidate 9:** $P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_1 + P^2 c_2 + Pc_3 + Pc_4 e^{Pc_5} + c_6 + c_7 e^{Pc_5}$

This gives: $c_0 P^3 + (c_1+c_2)P^2 + c_3 P + c_4 P e^{c_5 P} + c_6 + c_7 e^{c_5 P}$

GT has no constant term and no standalone $e^{-kP}$ term. Set $c_6 = 0$ and $c_7 = 0$. Then we get $c_0 P^3 + (c_1+c_2)P^2 + c_3 P + c_4 P e^{c_5 P}$.

Setting $c_5 = -k = -0.097$, $c_4 = -a = -0.17$, $c_0 = -a/(bd)$, $(c_1+c_2) = a/b$, $c_3 = a$.

This matches! GT = $c_0 P^3 + (c_1+c_2)P^2 + c_3 P + c_4 P e^{c_5 P}$.

**Candidate 9 matches the GT.**
